I've uploaded a python code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
Response to `SYS.REQ.USER.INFO` is missing 'permissions' field when request is serverd by the server that did not authenticate the user
### Observed behavior

Responses to `SYS.REQ.USER.INFO` sometimes would not have 'permissions' at all.
```
nats request -s nats://localhost:4222  --user alex --password pass  '$SYS.REQ.USER.INFO' ""  --raw 
{"server":{"name":"s2","host":"0.0.0.0","id":"NBULZKJORPE7OAR6CIGFFZJ2ZEOQYVGIMJFXSQGFQ6D5CIDD5SRTQ5RS","cluster":"proc_compose","ver":"2.12.0-dev","jetstream":false,"flags":0,"seq":874,"time":"2025-07-21T21:52:04.981771334Z"},"data":{"user":"alex","account":"ACC"}}
```

This happens when we got response not from the server that we are connected to.

I believe this happens because permissions that we return 
https://github.com/nats-io/nats-server/blob/5a574da4ec772c18502ed46ca73e148c26c7bc7c/server/events.go#L1501
https://github.com/nats-io/nats-server/blob/5a574da4ec772c18502ed46ca73e148c26c7bc7c/server/client.go#L1069

Are only set inside `processClientOrLeafAuthentication`: 
https://github.com/nats-io/nats-server/blob/5a574da4ec772c18502ed46ca73e148c26c7bc7c/server/auth.go#L1083
https://github.com/nats-io/nats-server/blob/5a574da4ec772c18502ed46ca73e148c26c7bc7c/server/client.go#L932-L938

And so when we get response from the server that did not Authenticate us, the permissions is nil, and so it is not present in the json response.

### Expected behavior

'permissions' is always present in the response, no matter which server served the request.

### Server and client version

main (2.11.6)

### Host environment

_No response_

### Steps to reproduce

I added a quick and dirty test to demonstrate:
```
git switch alex/test_SYS.REQ.USER.INFO
```

```
# go test -v  -timeout 30s  -run ^TestClusterClientUserInfoReq$ github.com/nats-io/nats-server/v2/server -count=1
```
The test will run until we get a response with missing permissions.

</pr_description>

  1168	        var ci ClientInfo
  1169

  1205	                                err = fmt.Errorf("%w at offset %d", err, syntaxErr.Offset)

  1207

Now I understand the issue. The problem is in line 1501 where we call `c.publicPermissions()` on the client that made the request (the service client handling the request), not on the actual user client whose information is being requested.

In a cluster scenario, when a request for user info is made, it can be handled by any server in the cluster. The `ci` (ClientInfo) contains information about the user (from line 1491), but the permissions are being read from `c` which is the system service client that's handling the request, not the actual user client.

   334	func (ci *ClientInfo) forAssignmentSnap() *ClientInfo {
   335	        return &ClientInfo{
   336	                Account: ci.Account,

   338	                Cluster: ci.Cluster,
   339	        }
   340	}
   341	
   342	// forProposal returns the minimum amount of ClientInfo we need for assignment proposals.
   343	func (ci *ClientInfo) forProposal() *ClientInfo {
   344	        if ci == nil {
   345	                return nil
   346	        }
   347	        cci := *ci
   348	        cci.Jwt = _EMPTY_
   349	        cci.IssuerKey = _EMPTY_
   350	        return &cci
   351	}

   356	                return nil
   357	        }

   359	        cci.Jwt = _EMPTY_
   360	        cci.Alternates = nil

+func TestClusterClientUserInfoReq(t *testing.T) {
+
+	jsClusterAccountsTempl := `
+	listen: 127.0.0.1:-1
+
+	server_name: %s
+	jetstream: {max_mem_store: 2GB, max_file_store: 2GB, store_dir: '%s'}
+
+	leaf {
+		listen: 127.0.0.1:-1
+	}
+
+	cluster {
+		name: %s
+		listen: 127.0.0.1:%d
+		routes = [%s]
+	}
+
+	websocket {
+		listen: 127.0.0.1:-1
+		compression: true
+		handshake_timeout: "5s"
+		no_tls: true
+	}
+
+	no_auth_user: dlc
+
+	
+		PERMS = {
+			publish = { allow: "$SYS.REQ.>", deny: "$SYS.REQ.ACCOUNT.>" }
+			subscribe = "_INBOX.>"
+			allow_responses: true
+		}
+	
+	accounts {
+		A: { users: [ { user: dlc, password: pass, permissions: $PERMS } ] }
+		ONE { users = [ { user: "one", pass: "p" }  ]; jetstream: enabled }
+		TWO { users = [ { user: "two", pass: "p" } ]; jetstream: enabled }
+		NOJS { users = [ { user: "nojs", pass: "p", permissions: $PERMS } ] }
+		$SYS { users = [ { user: "admin", pass: "s3cr3t!" } ] }
+	}
+`
+
+	// cluster := createJetStreamClusterExplicit(t, "test", 3)
+	cluster := createJetStreamClusterWithTemplate(t, jsClusterAccountsTempl, "test", 3)
+	defer cluster.shutdown()
+	cluster.waitOnClusterReady()
+
+	var i int
+	for {
+
+		s := cluster.randomServer()
+		nc, _ := jsClientConnect(t, s)
+		t.Logf("%d: Connected to %+v", i, nc.ConnectedServerName())
+		defer nc.Close()
+		resp, err := nc.Request("$SYS.REQ.USER.INFO", nil, time.Second)
+		require_NoError(t, err)
+
+		response := ServerAPIResponse{Data: &UserInfo{}}
+		err = json.Unmarshal(resp.Data, &response)
+		require_NoError(t, err)
+
+		userInfo := response.Data.(*UserInfo)
+
+		dlc := &UserInfo{
+			UserID:  "dlc",
+			Account: "A",
+			Permissions: &Permissions{
+				Publish: &SubjectPermission{
+					Allow: []string{"$SYS.REQ.>"},
+					Deny:  []string{"$SYS.REQ.ACCOUNT.>"},
+				},
+				Subscribe: &SubjectPermission{
+					Allow: []string{"_INBOX.>"},
+				},
+				Response: &ResponsePermission{
+					MaxMsgs: DEFAULT_ALLOW_RESPONSE_MAX_MSGS,
+					Expires: DEFAULT_ALLOW_RESPONSE_EXPIRATION,
+				},
+			},
+		}
+		if !reflect.DeepEqual(dlc, userInfo) {
+			t.Fatalf("User info for %q did not match. Got response: %+v from %s", "dlc", userInfo, response.Server.Name)
+		}
+		t.Logf("Got expected response %+v from %s", userInfo, response.Server.Name)
+		i++
+	}
+
+}

2025-12-26 19:51:11,859 - INFO - swea-agent-nats-io__nats-server-7089 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now I see the issue. The ClientInfo is created using `c.getClientInfo()` and marshaled into the request header. However, when looking back at the `getClientInfo` function (line 6049), I noticed that it doesn't include permissions. The permissions are only available on the actual client connection object (`c.perms`).

When the request is handled by the server that authenticated the user (where `c` is the actual user's client), `c.publicPermissions()` correctly returns the permissions. But when the request is handled by another server in the cluster, `c` is a system service client (not the original user's client), and its `perms` field is nil.

The solution is to:
1. Include permissions in the ClientInfo structure when it's propagated through headers
2. Modify the `userInfoReq` function to check if permissions exist in the ClientInfo header and use those if available

Let me first check if there are any security concerns with including permissions in ClientInfo:

2025-12-26 19:52:07,360 - INFO - swea-agent-nats-io__nats-server-7089 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now let me think about the solution. The issue is:

1. When a user makes a request to `$SYS.REQ.USER.INFO`, the request includes ClientInfo in the header.
2. This request can be serviced by any server in the cluster due to queue subscriptions.
3. The handler (`userInfoReq`) tries to get permissions from the client `c`, but `c` is the system service client on the server handling the request, not the original user's client.
4. The system service client has no permissions set (nil), so `c.publicPermissions()` returns nil.

The solution is to:
1. Add a `Permissions` field to `ClientInfo` struct
2. Populate it when creating ClientInfo for system imports
3. In `userInfoReq`, use the permissions from ClientInfo if available, otherwise fall back to `c.publicPermissions()`

Let me first look at how the ClientInfo is currently being created to understand where to add permissions:

\tUser       string        `json:"user,omitempty"`
\tName       string        `json:"name,omitempty"`
\tLang       string        `json:"lang,omitempty"`
\tVersion    string        `json:"ver,omitempty"`
\tRTT        time.Duration `json:"rtt,omitempty"`
\tServer     string        `json:"server,omitempty"`
\tCluster    string        `json:"cluster,omitempty"`
\tAlternates []string      `json:"alts,omitempty"`
\tStop       *time.Time    `json:"stop,omitempty"`
\tJwt        string        `json:"jwt,omitempty"`
\tIssuerKey  string        `json:"issuer_key,omitempty"`
\tNameTag    string        `json:"name_tag,omitempty"`
\tTags       jwt.TagList   `json:"tags,omitempty"`
\tKind       string        `json:"kind,omitempty"`
\tClientType string        `json:"client_type,omitempty"`
\tMQTTClient string        `json:"client_id,omitempty"` // This is the MQTT client ID
\tNonce      string        `json:"nonce,omitempty"`
}'''

new_struct = '''type ClientInfo struct {
\tStart       *time.Time    `json:"start,omitempty"`
\tHost        string        `json:"host,omitempty"`
\tID          uint64        `json:"id,omitempty"`
\tAccount     string        `json:"acc,omitempty"`
\tService     string        `json:"svc,omitempty"`
\tUser        string        `json:"user,omitempty"`
\tName        string        `json:"name,omitempty"`

\tNonce       string        `json:"nonce,omitempty"`
\tPermissions *Permissions  `json:"permissions,omitempty"`
}'''

if old_struct in content:
    content = content.replace(old_struct, new_struct)
    with open('server/events.go', 'w') as f:
        f.write(content)
    print("Successfully updated ClientInfo struct")
else:
    print("Could not find the exact pattern to replace")
    print("Trying a simpler approach...")

        print("Failed to update")

I see - `publicPermissions()` locks the client mutex itself. So I need to create a version that doesn't lock (since we're calling it while already holding the lock), or call it outside the lock. Let me look for a pattern in the code:

Actually, looking more carefully, I think a better approach is to call `c.publicPermissions()` before the lock in `getClientInfo()`, or to refactor `publicPermissions()` to have an unlocked version. However, the simplest solution is to call it after unlocking. Let me refactor `getClientInfo` to include permissions:

import re

with open('/testbed/server/client.go', 'r') as f:
    content = f.read()

# Find and replace the getClientInfo function
old_func = '''func (c *client) getClientInfo(detailed bool) *ClientInfo {
\tif c == nil || (c.kind != CLIENT && c.kind != LEAF && c.kind != JETSTREAM && c.kind != ACCOUNT) {
\t\treturn nil
\t}

\t// Result
\tvar ci ClientInfo

\tif detailed {
\t\tc.addServerAndClusterInfo(&ci)
\t}

\tc.mu.Lock()
\t// RTT and Account are always added.
\tci.Account = accForClient(c)
\tci.RTT = c.rtt
\t// Detailed signals additional opt in.
\tif detailed {
\t\tci.Start = &c.start
\t\tci.Host = c.host
\t\tci.ID = c.cid
\t\tci.Name = c.opts.Name
\t\tci.User = c.getRawAuthUser()
\t\tci.Lang = c.opts.Lang
\t\tci.Version = c.opts.Version
\t\tci.Jwt = c.opts.JWT
\t\tci.IssuerKey = issuerForClient(c)
\t\tci.NameTag = c.nameTag
\t\tci.Tags = c.tags
\t\tci.Kind = c.kindString()
\t\tci.ClientType = c.clientTypeString()
\t}
\tc.mu.Unlock()
\treturn &ci
}'''

new_func = '''func (c *client) getClientInfo(detailed bool) *ClientInfo {
\tif c == nil || (c.kind != CLIENT && c.kind != LEAF && c.kind != JETSTREAM && c.kind != ACCOUNT) {
\t\treturn nil
\t}

\t// Result
\tvar ci ClientInfo

\tif detailed {
\t\tc.addServerAndClusterInfo(&ci)
\t}

\tc.mu.Lock()
\t// RTT and Account are always added.
\tci.Account = accForClient(c)
\tci.RTT = c.rtt
\t// Detailed signals additional opt in.
\tif detailed {
\t\tci.Start = &c.start
\t\tci.Host = c.host
\t\tci.ID = c.cid
\t\tci.Name = c.opts.Name
\t\tci.User = c.getRawAuthUser()
\t\tci.Lang = c.opts.Lang
\t\tci.Version = c.opts.Version
\t\tci.Jwt = c.opts.JWT
\t\tci.IssuerKey = issuerForClient(c)
\t\tci.NameTag = c.nameTag
\t\tci.Tags = c.tags
\t\tci.Kind = c.kindString()
\t\tci.ClientType = c.clientTypeString()
\t}
\tc.mu.Unlock()
\t// Add permissions. This needs to be done after unlocking since
\t// publicPermissions() also acquires the lock.
\tif detailed {
\t\tci.Permissions = c.publicPermissions()
\t}
\treturn &ci
}'''

if old_func in content:
    content = content.replace(old_func, new_func)
    with open('/testbed/server/client.go', 'w') as f:
        f.write(content)
    print("Successfully updated getClientInfo function")
else:
    print("Could not find exact match")

# Find and replace the userInfoReq function

func (s *Server) userInfoReq(sub *subscription, c *client, _ *Account, subject, reply string, msg []byte) {

\t\treturn
\t}

\t}

\tresponse := &ServerAPIResponse{Server: &ServerInfo{}}

\tci, _, _, _, err := s.getRequestInfo(c, msg)
\tif err != nil {
\t\tresponse.Error = &ApiError{Code: http.StatusBadRequest}
\t\ts.sendInternalResponse(reply, response)
\t\treturn
\t}

\t// Use permissions from ClientInfo if available (when request is forwarded
\t// from another server in the cluster), otherwise get from the client connection.
\tperms := ci.Permissions
\tif perms == nil {
\t\tperms = c.publicPermissions()
\t}

\tresponse.Data = &UserInfo{
\t\tUserID:      ci.User,
\t\tAccount:     ci.Account,
\t\tPermissions: perms,
\t\tExpires:     c.claimExpiration(),
\t}
\ts.sendInternalResponse(reply, response)
}'''

if old_func in content:
    content = content.replace(old_func, new_func)
    with open('/testbed/server/events.go', 'w') as f:
        f.write(content)
    print("Successfully updated userInfoReq function")
else:
    print("Could not find exact match")

	"fmt"
	"reflect"
	"time"

	"github.com/nats-io/nats.go"
)

type ServerAPIResponse struct {
	Server *ServerInfo `json:"server"`
	Data   interface{} `json:"data,omitempty"`
	Error  *ApiError   `json:"error,omitempty"`
}

type ServerInfo struct {
	Name      string    `json:"name"`
	Host      string    `json:"host"`
	ID        string    `json:"id"`
	Cluster   string    `json:"cluster,omitempty"`
	Version   string    `json:"ver"`
	Seq       uint64    `json:"seq"`
	JetStream bool      `json:"jetstream"`
	Time      time.Time `json:"time"`
}

type ApiError struct {
	Code        int    `json:"code"`
	ErrCode     int    `json:"err_code,omitempty"`
	Description string `json:"description,omitempty"`
}

type UserInfo struct {
	UserID      string        `json:"user"`
	Account     string        `json:"account"`
	Permissions *Permissions  `json:"permissions,omitempty"`
	Expires     time.Duration `json:"expires,omitempty"`
}

type Permissions struct {
	Publish   *SubjectPermission  `json:"publish"`
	Subscribe *SubjectPermission  `json:"subscribe"`
	Response  *ResponsePermission `json:"responses,omitempty"`
}

type SubjectPermission struct {
	Allow []string `json:"allow,omitempty"`
	Deny  []string `json:"deny,omitempty"`
}

type ResponsePermission struct {
	MaxMsgs int           `json:"max"`
	Expires time.Duration `json:"ttl"`
}

const DEFAULT_ALLOW_RESPONSE_MAX_MSGS = 1
const DEFAULT_ALLOW_RESPONSE_EXPIRATION = 2 * time.Second

func main() {
	// Connect to one of the servers
	// Using dlc/pass credentials from test config
	nc, err := nats.Connect("nats://127.0.0.1:4222", nats.UserInfo("dlc", "pass"))
	if err != nil {
		fmt.Printf("Failed to connect: %v\n", err)
		return
	}
	defer nc.Close()

	for i := 0; i < 100; i++ {
		resp, err := nc.Request("$SYS.REQ.USER.INFO", nil, time.Second)
		if err != nil {
			fmt.Printf("Request failed: %v\n", err)
			continue
		}

		var response ServerAPIResponse
		response.Data = &UserInfo{}
		err = json.Unmarshal(resp.Data, &response)
		if err != nil {
			fmt.Printf("Failed to unmarshal: %v\n", err)
			continue
		}

		userInfo := response.Data.(*UserInfo)

		expectedPerms := &Permissions{
			Publish: &SubjectPermission{
				Allow: []string{"$SYS.REQ.>"},
				Deny:  []string{"$SYS.REQ.ACCOUNT.>"},
			},
			Subscribe: &SubjectPermission{
				Allow: []string{"_INBOX.>"},
			},
			Response: &ResponsePermission{
				MaxMsgs: DEFAULT_ALLOW_RESPONSE_MAX_MSGS,
				Expires: DEFAULT_ALLOW_RESPONSE_EXPIRATION,
			},
		}

		if userInfo.Permissions == nil {
			fmt.Printf("FAIL: Iteration %d - Permissions is nil! Response from server: %s\n", i, response.Server.Name)
			return
		}

		if !reflect.DeepEqual(expectedPerms, userInfo.Permissions) {
			fmt.Printf("FAIL: Iteration %d - Permissions don't match. Got: %+v, Expected: %+v from server: %s\n",
				i, userInfo.Permissions, expectedPerms, response.Server.Name)
			return
		}

		fmt.Printf("PASS: Iteration %d - Got correct response from server: %s\n", i, response.Server.Name)
	}

	fmt.Println("\nAll 100 iterations passed!")
}

So our fix should work! The permissions should be included in the ClientInfo when it's marshaled and sent in the header. Then on the receiving server, when `userInfoReq` is called:
1. It parses the ClientInfo from the header (line 1492)

3. If yes, it uses those; otherwise, it falls back to `c.publicPermissions()`

#!/bin/bash
cd /testbed

# Run the test with a timeout - if it runs beyond 10 seconds, the test is passing
# (the original test had an infinite loop that would exit when it found missing permissions)
timeout 10s go test -v -timeout 30s -run ^TestClusterClientUserInfoReq$ github.com/nats-io/nats-server/v2/server -count=1 2>&1 &
TEST_PID=$!

sleep 8

# If the test is still running after 8 seconds, it's likely passing (infinite loop means it's working)
if ps -p $TEST_PID > /dev/null 2>&1; then
    echo "Test is still running after 8 seconds - likely passing!"
    kill -9 $TEST_PID 2>/dev/null
    exit 0
else
    wait $TEST_PID
    EXIT_CODE=$?
    if [ $EXIT_CODE -eq 0 ]; then
        echo "Test completed successfully!"
        exit 0
    else
        echo "Test failed with exit code $EXIT_CODE"
        exit 1
    fi
fi
EOF
chmod +x /tmp/test_fix.sh

func TestClientUserInfoReq(t *testing.T) {
	conf := createConfFile(t, []byte(`
		listen: 127.0.0.1:-1
		PERMS = {
			publish = { allow: "$SYS.REQ.>", deny: "$SYS.REQ.ACCOUNT.>" }
			subscribe = "_INBOX.>"
			allow_responses: true
		}
		accounts: {
			A: { users: [ { user: dlc, password: pass, permissions: $PERMS } ] }
			$SYS { users = [ { user: "admin", pass: "s3cr3t!" } ] }
		}
		no_auth_user: dlc
	`))
	defer removeFile(t, conf)

	s, _ := RunServerWithConfig(conf)
	defer s.Shutdown()

	nc, err := nats.Connect(s.ClientURL())
	require_NoError(t, err)
	defer nc.Close()

	resp, err := nc.Request("$SYS.REQ.USER.INFO", nil, time.Second)
	require_NoError(t, err)

	response := ServerAPIResponse{Data: &UserInfo{}}
	err = json.Unmarshal(resp.Data, &response)
	require_NoError(t, err)

	userInfo := response.Data.(*UserInfo)

	dlc := &UserInfo{
		UserID:  "dlc",
		Account: "A",
		Permissions: &Permissions{
			Publish: &SubjectPermission{
				Allow: []string{"$SYS.REQ.>"},
				Deny:  []string{"$SYS.REQ.ACCOUNT.>"},
			},
			Subscribe: &SubjectPermission{
				Allow: []string{"_INBOX.>"},
			},
			Response: &ResponsePermission{
				MaxMsgs: DEFAULT_ALLOW_RESPONSE_MAX_MSGS,
				Expires: DEFAULT_ALLOW_RESPONSE_EXPIRATION,
			},
		},
	}
	if !reflect.DeepEqual(dlc, userInfo) {
		t.Fatalf("User info for %q did not match", "dlc")
